term='shark movie'/><title type='text'>Here is your chance to make your own shark diving movie!</title><content type='html'>Have you ever dreamed of diving with &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com//bookings/"&gt;great white sharks&lt;/a&gt;? Did you ever want to know, how they film those amazing underwater scenes you see in the movie theaters and on television?&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This is your chance to do both! Join &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/dive-packages/great-white-shark-diving-film-expedition/"&gt;Shark Diver&lt;/a&gt;&lt;b&gt; &lt;/b&gt;and Emmy award winning underwater cinematographer Peter Kragh at the peak of &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/dive-packages/great-white-shark-diving-film-expedition/"&gt;Guadalupe Island&lt;/a&gt;'s&lt;b&gt; &lt;/b&gt;shark  season, to dive with great white sharks and learn about the many facets of underwater documentary film  making. Whether you are just an amateur or an emerging filmmaker, this  is an opportunity to get some expert advise on how to make your videos and, of  course, come eye to eye with some of the greatest sharks in the world.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/01/Peter-Kragh.jpg" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://www.sharkdiver.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/01/Peter-Kragh.jpg" height="212" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;Peter Kragh&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;Peter is intimately familiar with sharks. He has  filmed everything from little horn sharks to whale sharks and great  whites and worked on many Shark Week episodes. He will be there to help  you improve your photography skills and experience. There will also be  screenings of some of Peters work. With all the dives he's done around the world, Peter can also help you find that "secret" location  for your next diving adventure.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Here is a short video, showcasing Peter's work.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;iframe allowfullscreen="" frameborder="0" height="281" mozallowfullscreen="" src="//player.vimeo.com/video/94559582" webkitallowfullscreen="" width="500"&gt;&lt;/iframe&gt; &lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://vimeo.com/94559582"&gt;Demo Reel 2014&lt;/a&gt; from &lt;a href="http://vimeo.com/peterkragh"&gt;Peter Kragh&lt;/a&gt; on &lt;a href="https://vimeo.com/"&gt;Vimeo&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;As  a professional cameraman for over 10 years, Peter has worked on well  known BBC and National Geographic projects like Blue Planet, Planet  Earth, Life and Secret Life of Predators. In 2013 he won an Emmy award  for outstanding cinematography on the Nat Geo series "Untamed Americas".  He has also worked on multiple Imax films: Deep Sea 3D, Hubble 3D,  Under The Sea 3D, and Journey to the South Pacific 3D.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;With  all this experience, Peter will sure be able to help you make your own amazing video, to document your trip of a lifetime. This is a unique opportunity to both improve  your filming skills, while having the time of your life, coming face to  face with the &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/dive-packages/great-white-shark-diving/"&gt;Great White Sharks&lt;/a&gt; at &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/tv"&gt;Guadalupe Island&lt;/a&gt;!&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/tv"&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-Mw5BoT_RGOg/UiEE9Oj_EgI/AAAAAAAAAOo/SgKe0QWz41I/s1600/%2356.jpg" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-Mw5BoT_RGOg/UiEE9Oj_EgI/AAAAAAAAAOo/SgKe0QWz41I/s1600/%2356.jpg" height="240" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The video below is from last season, shot without Peter's assistance. I can't wait to see, how much better it will be with his help this year!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;object width="320" term='stupid &quot;scientist&quot;'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='Shark diving'/><title type='text'>New shark research method?</title><content type='html'>&lt;div id="line1"&gt;&lt;span style="background-color: white;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;"Are you sure he only eats plankton? Daring marine biologist hitches a ride on the world's largest shark"&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt; &lt;/span&gt;is the headline of the &lt;a href="http://www.dailymail.co.uk/"&gt;"Mail Online"&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div id="line1"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div id="line1"&gt;Combining the term "marine biologist" and riding sharks peaked my curiosity. Has someone found out that riding sharks is beneficial to them? Have I been wrong all these years, condemning that practice? &lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div id="line1"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div id="line1"&gt;&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt;The article started out with &lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;"Marine biologist Forrest Galante has swam  with some of the most fearsome creatures in the sea, including the  terrifying hammerhead." &lt;/i&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;So immediately I realized, this is a highly scientific article and thankfully they're not going to use sensationalistic language. (sharkasm intended!) "Terrifying Hammerhead" indeed.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div style="background-color: white; border: medium none; color: black; overflow: hidden; text-align: left; text-decoration: none;"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;In this picture you see the "heroic" Forrest Galante in his death defying act of riding a 45 ft. whale shark!&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div style="background-color: white; border: medium none; color: black; overflow: hidden; text-align: left; text-decoration: none;"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://i.dailymail.co.uk/i/pix/2015/03/19/26CAD1A200000578-0-image-a-75_1426781666654.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://i.dailymail.co.uk/i/pix/2015/03/19/26CAD1A200000578-0-image-a-75_1426781666654.jpg" height="180" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div id="line1"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div id="line1"&gt;The caption for the picture below reads&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;"Galante and his team were measuring the giant "whales" who were returning to the secret Mexican location."&amp;nbsp;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div id="line1"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://i.dailymail.co.uk/i/pix/2015/03/19/26CAD15500000578-0-image-a-73_1426781463081.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://i.dailymail.co.uk/i/pix/2015/03/19/26CAD15500000578-0-image-a-73_1426781463081.jpg" height="173" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I have to admit that I'm not a scientist. Apparently I know even less than I previously assumed. Who know what whale sharks are "whales"? And the secret location? Is it Isla Mujeres? We wouldn't want them to start a whale shark watching industry &lt;a href="https://www.google.com/search?q=isla+mujeres+whale+sharks&amp;amp;ie=utf-8&amp;amp;oe=utf-8"&gt;there&lt;/a&gt;. Or maybe it's Baja California? Same thing, I hope nobody starts whale shark watching &lt;a href="https://www.google.com/search?q=baja+california+whale+shark&amp;amp;ie=utf-8&amp;amp;oe=utf-8"&gt;there&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So what was this research that the local marine biologists needed his expert help with anyway? &lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt;"I was helping out a team of marine  biologists conduct a survey on whale shark population estimates, to  identify returning sharks year on year and to see growth rates of  individuals."&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt; No wonder he needed to ride those sharks! I mean, how else could you measure a shark than by riding it. The watch you see on his wrist must be a super secret measuring device!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Anyway, no matter how hard I tried, I couldn't find any other references to anything remotely research related in the article &lt;a href="http://www.dailymail.co.uk/news/article-3002761/Are-sure-eats-plankton-Marine-biologist-hitches-ride-world-s-largest-shark.html"&gt;here&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I did however find the real reason for Galante's antics. On &lt;a href="https://www.facebook.com/ForrestGalante/posts/1631945437025515"&gt;his facebook page&lt;/a&gt; he writes &lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;"Hey I'm back in the &lt;a class="_58cn" data-ft="{&amp;quot;tn&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;*N&amp;quot;,&amp;quot;type&amp;quot;:104}" href="https://www.facebook.com/hashtag/news?source=feed_text&amp;amp;story_id=1631945437025515"&gt;&lt;span class="_58cl"&gt;‪#‎&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="_58cm"&gt;news‬&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;! so proud to have been a part of it!&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div style="background-color: white; border: medium none; color: black; overflow: hidden; text-align: left; text-decoration: none;"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div style="background-color: white; border: medium none; color: black; overflow: hidden; text-align: left; text-decoration: none;"&gt;Just as I thought, it's all about him. width: 100%;"&gt;&lt;div style="height: 0; padding-bottom: 100%; padding-top: 25px; position: relative;"&gt;&lt;iframe src="//fatal-shark-attacks-off-the-california-coast.silk.co/s/embed/map/collection/fatal-shark-attacks-off-california-coast/column/description/location/address" style="border: 0; in 115 years, there have been only 13 unprovoked fatal shark attacks and none since 2008. It must be a really slow news day in Los Angeles, that they have to use this sensationalistic headline, with the last shark fatality having occurred over 6 years ago.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;It is ridiculous, using data and maps along with misleading headlines like this. class="hasCaption"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;br /&gt; On the 5 march 2015 a government council banned the Import of fins into the country. The Swiss national council accepted the proposition on thursday by 160 votes against 19 and was passed into effect. Amazing!&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;span class="fbPhotosPhotoCaption" data-ft="{&amp;quot;tn&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;K&amp;quot;}" id="fbPhotoSnowliftCaption" tabindex="0"&gt;&lt;span class="hasCaption"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="fbPhotosPhotoCaption" data-ft="{&amp;quot;tn&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;K&amp;quot;}" id="fbPhotoSnowliftCaption" tabindex="0"&gt;&lt;span class="hasCaption"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt; &lt;/i&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Just goes to show that the tired old excuse of contravening World Trading Standards - is a load of rubbish.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span class="fbPhotosPhotoCaption" data-ft="{&amp;quot;tn&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;K&amp;quot;}" id="fbPhotoSnowliftCaption" tabindex="0"&gt;&lt;span class="hasCaption"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;That certainly sounds like good news. Anytime a country decides to ban the importation of &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;shark&lt;/a&gt; fins, it is a victory for sharks. Since I grew up in Switzerland and obviously love sharks, I wanted to find out, a bit more about the process of how this law was passed and just how many sharks might be saved by it. What I found out might surprise you.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span class="fbPhotosPhotoCaption" data-ft="{&amp;quot;tn&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;K&amp;quot;}" id="fbPhotoSnowliftCaption" tabindex="0"&gt;&lt;span class="hasCaption"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;According to the official website for the &lt;a href="http://www.admin.ch/"&gt;Swiss Government&lt;/a&gt;, the motion to establish this law was registered on April 17, 2013, &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="fbPhotosPhotoCaption" data-ft="{&amp;quot;tn&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;K&amp;quot;}" id="fbPhotoSnowliftCaption" tabindex="0"&gt;&lt;span class="hasCaption"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;&lt;span class="fbPhotosPhotoCaption" data-ft="{&amp;quot;tn&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;K&amp;quot;}" id="fbPhotoSnowliftCaption" tabindex="0"&gt;&lt;span class="hasCaption"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;by Congressman &lt;a href="https://www.facebook.com/pages/Oskar-Freysinger/139479089463165"&gt;Oskar Freysinger.&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt; That means this process took about 2 years. Surprising many, the Swiss Federal Council, (the executive branch) was opposed to the ban, partially because of international trade agreements, which &lt;a href="http://www.finfighters.org/#home1"&gt;Fin Fighters&lt;/a&gt; mentioned as a ridiculous excuse. &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="fbPhotosPhotoCaption" data-ft="{&amp;quot;tn&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;K&amp;quot;}" id="fbPhotoSnowliftCaption" tabindex="0"&gt;&lt;span class="hasCaption"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;The main reason for their opposition was entirely different though. According to the Swiss import statistics, no shark fins are being imported into Switzerland, negating the need for a law. &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span class="fbPhotosPhotoCaption" data-ft="{&amp;quot;tn&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;K&amp;quot;}" id="fbPhotoSnowliftCaption" tabindex="0"&gt;&lt;span class="hasCaption"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;I have to say that I'm proud of the country I grew up in. Not only do they now officially ban the import of shark fins, they never consumed them in the first place. At least not in quantities that would show up in import statistics.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span class="fbPhotosPhotoCaption" data-ft="{&amp;quot;tn&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;K&amp;quot;}" id="fbPhotoSnowliftCaption" tabindex="0"&gt;&lt;span class="hasCaption"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Of course, anytime a country decides to pass a law like this, there are numerous groups either claiming credit and/or are using the news for fundraising. In the case of Switzerland, it was the initiative of just one Congressman, Mr. &lt;a href="https://www.facebook.com/pages/Oskar-Freysinger/139479089463165"&gt;Oskar Freysinger.&lt;/a&gt; &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="fbPhotosPhotoCaption" data-ft="{&amp;quot;tn&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;K&amp;quot;}" id="fbPhotoSnowliftCaption" tabindex="0"&gt;&lt;span class="hasCaption"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Merci bien, Oscar!&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span class="fbPhotosPhotoCaption" data-ft="{&amp;quot;tn&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;K&amp;quot;}" id="fbPhotoSnowliftCaption" tabindex="0"&gt;&lt;span class="hasCaption"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Cheers,&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span class="fbPhotosPhotoCaption" data-ft="{&amp;quot;tn&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;K&amp;quot;}" id="fbPhotoSnowliftCaption" tabindex="0"&gt;&lt;span class="hasCaption"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Martin Graf&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span class="fbPhotosPhotoCaption" data-ft="{&amp;quot;tn&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;K&amp;quot;}" id="fbPhotoSnowliftCaption" tabindex="0"&gt;&lt;span class="hasCaption"&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;CEO Shark Diver &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.   As a global leader in commercial shark diving and conservation initiatives Shark Diver has spent the past decade engaged for sharks around the world. Our blog highlights all aspects of both of these dynamic and shifting worlds. You can reach us directly at staff@sharkdiver.com.</content><link rel='replies' type='application/atom+xml' href='https://sharkdivers.blogspot.com/feeds/898225358419556810/comments/default' title='Post Comments'/><link rel='replies' type='text/html' href='https://www.blogger.com/comment.g?blogID=370711998877298323&amp;postID=898225358419556810' title='0 Comments'/><link rel='edit' type='application/atom+xml' href='https://www.blogger.com/feeds/370711998877298323/posts/default/898225358419556810'/><link rel='self' type='application/atom+xml' href='https://www.blogger.com/feeds/370711998877298323/posts/default/898225358419556810'/><link rel='alternate' type='text/html' href='http://sharkdivers.blogspot.com/2015/03/switzerland-bans-importation-of-shark.html' title='Switzerland bans the importation of shark fins!'/><author><name>Shark Diver</name><uri>https://plus.google.com/107965598445039841723</uri><email>noreply@blogger.com</email><gd:image rel='http://schemas.google.com/g/2005#thumbnail' width='32' height='32' src='//lh5.googleusercontent.com/-acNbaifFSTQ/AAAAAAAAAAI/AAAAAAAAB_A/inqVjDI-1J8/s32-c/photo.jpg'/></author><thr:total>0</thr:total></entry><entry><id>tag:blogger.com,1999:blog-370711998877298323.post-3683148548135153131</id><published>2015-03-10T19:44:00.000-07:00</published><updated>2015-03-10T19:44:23.636-07:00</updated><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='shark diver'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='stupid diver'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='stupid media'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='swimming with sharks'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='hammerhead shark'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='Shark diving'/><title type='text'>Hammerhead shark attacking diver?</title><content type='html'>As shark &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;diving operators&lt;/a&gt; we have to be aware of our actions and how they are depicted in the media. Every time something goes wrong, or someone get's a sensationalistic video of a shark dive, the shark gets portrayed as a bloodthirsty manhunter!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-B0J646Acr7Q/VP-pnTb9vAI/AAAAAAAABUA/Yh95jrtRXBI/s1600/DSC_0117.JPG" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-B0J646Acr7Q/VP-pnTb9vAI/AAAAAAAABUA/Yh95jrtRXBI/s1600/DSC_0117.JPG" height="212" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Take this latest report on &lt;a href="http://msn.com/"&gt;MSN&lt;/a&gt;, reporting &lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;"&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-weight: normal;"&gt;Hammerhead shark tries to attack diver"&amp;nbsp; &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt;and all the way from Australia, &lt;a href="http://www.9news.com.au/"&gt;news 9&lt;/a&gt; writes &lt;span style="color: #990000;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;"Daring diver taunts angry shark!"&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt; &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-weight: normal;"&gt;Yes, daring, cool, courageous diver is confronting and angry man killer! So what happened?&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-weight: normal;"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-weight: normal;"&gt;Well, watch the video below and you'll see for yourself.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.newsflare.com/video/41672/travel/hammerhead-shark-tries-to-attack-diver"&gt;&lt;span style="font-size: small;"&gt;&lt;span style="font-weight: normal;"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.newsflare.com/video/41672/travel/hammerhead-shark-tries-to-attack-diver"&gt;http://www.newsflare.com/video/41672/travel/hammerhead-shark-tries-to-attack-diver&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&amp;nbsp; &lt;br /&gt;Basically we have a diver with a piece of fish in his right hand, not wearing any chainlink glove or any other protective gear, standing right next to a bait box. When the hammerhead approaches the diver, trying to get the fish, the diver grabs it's head and pushes it around. You notice that the first guy who was feeding the shark is actually turning it's back to this "angry" shark. That alone gives you an indication of how "responsible" this outfit is. You'll also see that the only diver the shark is interested in, is the one with the fish in his hand and not the "tasty rubber suited human" as news 9 would have you.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-2ulQ_JugqJM/VP-ppuda8qI/AAAAAAAABUI/9bHVP3f1xeo/s1600/DSC_0126.JPG" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-2ulQ_JugqJM/VP-ppuda8qI/AAAAAAAABUI/9bHVP3f1xeo/s1600/DSC_0126.JPG" height="212" width="320" /&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;News 9 writes &lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;"As hard as the shark tries, it just can't  get close enough to the tasty rubber-suited human to take a chunk out of  him, and the diver seems to know it."&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Read the entire news 9 article &lt;a href="http://www.9news.com.au/world/2015/03/10/10/50/daring-diver-taunts-angry-hammerhead"&gt;here&lt;/a&gt; and MSN's video &lt;a href="http://www.msn.com/en-us/video/football_nfl/hammerhead-shark-tries-to-attack-diver/vi-AA9y6Uv"&gt;here&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;It's not just the media though. In an effort to make money off the video, the diver who shot it, advertises it like this&lt;span style="color: #45818e;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="color: #45818e;"&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: #45818e;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.newsflare.com/video/41672/travel/hammerhead-shark-tries-to-attack-diver"&gt;&lt;i&gt;"&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: #45818e;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.newsflare.com/video/41672/travel/hammerhead-shark-tries-to-attack-diver"&gt;Hammerhead shark tries to attack diver! A dramatic video has emerged of a hammerhead shark trying to attack a diver in the Bahamas. In the footage, captured during a scuba diving trip in the Bimini Atoll in late January, the shark can be seen circling a diver before lunging forwards several times. Fortunately, the experienced diver &lt;span&gt;was able to push the shark away and survived the experience without any injuries."&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;i&gt; &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&amp;nbsp; &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;We at &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Shark Diver&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;i&gt; &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;practice "safe and sane" &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/dive-packages/tiger-shark-diving/"&gt;shark diving&lt;/a&gt;. Along with the many responsible shark diving outfits out there, we are aware of our responsibility to treat the &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;sharks&lt;/a&gt; with respect and portray them in a realistic light. You won't find us riding, hugging or flipping them, we respect them to be awesome predators that are not trying to eat us, but are neither trying to be hugged by us. We are not trying to tease the shark with a piece of fish in our hand and then call it an attack, when the shark tries to get to eat the fish.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-ceR7MHHtW-E/VP-fj6vd5SI/AAAAAAAABTw/mt1010bCsxM/s1600/IMG_5746%2B-%2BCopy.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-ceR7MHHtW-E/VP-fj6vd5SI/AAAAAAAABTw/mt1010bCsxM/s1600/IMG_5746%2B-%2BCopy.jpg" height="213" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;We get close to the sharks, but we don't hug them! We are aware that if anything bad happens during a shark dive, the sharks will get blamed and not the irresponsible divers and operators. If you want to know who the operator of this particular dive was, just watch the video. It's name is prominently displayed on the bait box!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Let's go shark diving! Responsibly!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cheers,&lt;br /&gt;Martin Graf&lt;br /&gt;CEO Shark Diver&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. term='great white shark'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='diving with sharks'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='Shark diving'/><title type='text'>Are white sharks parenting their offspring?</title><content type='html'>When it comes to how the media covers any sightings of a great white shark, it never ceases to amaze me how their articles are devoid of any real facts and full of disinformation. Take this latest coverage by the &lt;a href="http://www.inquisitr.com/"&gt;Inquisitr&lt;/a&gt; of a sighting in lake Macquarie. You really have to wonder who these experts are, that they refer to in &lt;a href="http://www.inquisitr.com/1898366/great-white-shark-returns-to-lake-macquarie-and-it-brought-a-friend/"&gt;this&lt;/a&gt; article.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;They are saying&amp;nbsp; &lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;"A 9-foot-long great white shark has been  spotted in Australia’s Lake Macquarie, close to the scene of another  recent sighting, along with a smaller, unidentified fish that some  researchers believe could be the shark’s offspring".&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/--3jbz3rwnfs/UvaMpo_Zc0I/AAAAAAAAAtI/dqfwfkjoLoA/s1600/email%2B4.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/--3jbz3rwnfs/UvaMpo_Zc0I/AAAAAAAAAtI/dqfwfkjoLoA/s1600/email%2B4.jpg" height="219" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="copy-paste-block"&gt;&lt;span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="copy-paste-block"&gt;&lt;span&gt;Now I have to say that even though I'm not a scientist, but simply a guy who's been diving with &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;great white sharks&lt;/a&gt; at &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/tv"&gt;Isla Guadalupe&lt;/a&gt; for 14 years, I do know that a 9 ft &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/dive-packages/great-white-shark-diving/"&gt;great white shark&lt;/a&gt; is not sexually mature and thus cannot have an offspring.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cheers,&lt;br /&gt;Martin Graf&lt;br /&gt;CEO &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Shark Diver&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.   As a global leader in commercial shark diving and conservation initiatives Shark Diver has spent the past decade engaged for sharks around the world. Our blog highlights all aspects of both of these dynamic and shifting worlds. You can reach us directly at staff@sharkdiver.com.</content><link rel='replies' type='application/atom+xml' href='https://sharkdivers.blogspot.com/feeds/8183432953149200287/comments/default' title='Post Comments'/><link rel='replies' type='text/html' href='https://www.blogger.com/comment.g?blogID=370711998877298323&amp;postID=8183432953149200287' title='0 Comments'/><link rel='edit' type='application/atom+xml' href='https://www.blogger.com/feeds/370711998877298323/posts/default/8183432953149200287'/><link rel='self' type='application/atom+xml' href='https://www.blogger.com/feeds/370711998877298323/posts/default/8183432953149200287'/><link rel='alternate' type='text/html' href='http://sharkdivers.blogspot.com/2015/03/are-white-sharks-parenting-their.html' title='Are white sharks parenting their offspring?'/><author><name>Shark Diver</name><uri>https://plus.google.com/107965598445039841723</uri><email>noreply@blogger.com</email><gd:image rel='http://schemas.google.com/g/2005#thumbnail' width='32' height='32' src='//lh5.googleusercontent.com/-acNbaifFSTQ/AAAAAAAAAAI/AAAAAAAAB_A/inqVjDI-1J8/s32-c/photo.jpg'/></author><media:thumbnail xmlns:media='http://search.yahoo.com/mrss/' url='http://1.bp.blogspot.com/--3jbz3rwnfs/UvaMpo_Zc0I/AAAAAAAAAtI/dqfwfkjoLoA/s72-c/email%2B4.jpg' height='72' width='72'/><thr:total>0</thr:total></entry><entry><id>tag:blogger.com,1999:blog-370711998877298323.post-7773529821352861027</id><published>2015-03-06T08:57:00.000-08:00</published><updated>2015-03-06T08:57:34.391-08:00</updated><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='cool critters'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='goblin shark'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='deep ocean'/><title type='text'>Really cool shark!</title><content type='html'>You never know what you are going to find in the ocean. We know more about the moon, than we do about the creatures in the ocean. scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='bull shark'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='great hammerhead shark'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='dead shark'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='shark finning'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='Miami Beach'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='shark media'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='great white shark'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='selfies'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='shark fin soup'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='Shark diving'/><title type='text'>Dead Sharks, Selfies, and Shark Fin Soup?</title><content type='html'>&lt;h2&gt;&lt;/h2&gt;What is our obsession with taking pictures of ourselves with subjects that seem just a bit inappropriate? Now that smart phones have turned us all into photog wannabes, the rush to get pictures published on social media sites has also lead us to be wannabe reporters, as well.&amp;nbsp; Recently two &lt;a href="http://sharkdiver.com/"&gt;sharks&lt;/a&gt;, a &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/dive-packages/bull-shark-diving-fiji/"&gt;bull &lt;/a&gt;and a hammerhead, washed up dead on the shore of &lt;a href="http://www.miamibeachfl.gov/"&gt;Miami Beach&lt;/a&gt;. One was bloated, the other with its fin cut off.&amp;nbsp; Once beach-combers saw the poor creatures, the camera phones came out and the snap-shot taking crowds were enough to make any paparazzi, surrounding a Hollywood celebrity, pale in comparison.&amp;nbsp; There was even a grown adult who pulled up on the head of one &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;shark&lt;/a&gt; to get its mouth to open. What a photo op! "Hey kids, come gather around!"&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;span style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.wsvn.com/story/28203396/dead-bullshark-washes-up-on-miami-beach"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-ofm_zNTwTOM/VPXn1WfPySI/AAAAAAAABSs/-CabYPZUYLI/s1600/Screen%2BShot%2B2015-03-03%2Bat%2B11.46.14%2BAM.png" height="237" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Where is the respect? It’s just an animal. Who cares, right? WRONG! Are we another 'Me Generation' or have we never left it? &amp;nbsp;This is 2015 folks.&amp;nbsp; We've scratched our way out to escape the errors of our ways. After fighting for equality in several different arenas, freedom of religion, the push to reuse, reduce and recycle, ‘save our planet,’ ‘plant a tree’…have we not arrived? What has happened to the rights and respect for those with which we share this slowly, dying planet?&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;img alt="http://cdn.inquisitr.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/02/Bull-Shark-670.jpg" border="0" src="http://cdn.inquisitr.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/02/Bull-Shark-670.jpg" height="195" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;Source: Inquisitr.com&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://cdn.inquisitr.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/02/Bull-Shark-670.jpg"&gt;&lt;span id="goog_446680597"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;span id="goog_446680598"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Back to these dead sharks: No one knows what caused their deaths, and apparently no one is investigating.&amp;nbsp; A fin was cut off! I was told by an authority at the &lt;a href="http://myfwc.com/"&gt;Florida Fish and Wildlife Conservation Commission&lt;/a&gt; that maybe if there was a bunch of these guys washing up on the shore with their fins hacked, there might then be an investigation. How many have to lose their lives in order for that to happen? Maybe this is just a prelude of what is to come. Since &lt;i&gt;shark fin soup&lt;/i&gt; is served in restaurants throughout &lt;a href="http://www.visitflorida.com/en-us.html"&gt;Florida&lt;/a&gt;, and yes, &lt;a href="http://www.miamigov.com/home/"&gt;Miami&lt;/a&gt;, maybe this was the result of someone trying to cash in on the evil craze. Does that mean finless carcasses are on their way to shore like a message in a bottle? Are we going to read it and do something about it or are we going to throw it back in for the next generation to deal with? Did you know that 24 states according to the &lt;a href="https://awionline.org/content/restaurants-currently-offering-shark-fin-soup"&gt;Animal Welfare Institute&lt;/a&gt;, serve up the controversial delicacy, &lt;i&gt;shark fin soup&lt;/i&gt;?&amp;nbsp; You can find it on the menu at South Garden Chinese Restaurant in &lt;a href="http://www.miamigov.com/home/"&gt;Miami&lt;/a&gt; for $12 a bowl.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="https://pbs.twimg.com/media/B-t2rnkXEAAbG8f.png:large" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="230" src="https://pbs.twimg.com/media/B-t2rnkXEAAbG8f.png:large" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="https://twitter.com/earthrace/status/570681383347208194/photo/1"&gt;Source&lt;/a&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;br /&gt;It’s a shame; it’s a crying shame that an 8 foot animal is tortured for its 8 inch body part and left to die, rotting in its ocean home, only to float to the shore to be mocked as part of social media fodder. To the person(s) who did this: "At least, eat the rest!" I discourage anyone from killing these animals and it pains me to see their fins cut off and then the shark dropped back in the water to try and survive. Would the same thoughtless individual do that to their pet? They’d be put in jail.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;These sharks are intelligent, beautiful, and are an integral part of our oceans and were here way before you and I. Respect them. Wouldn't a picture of you with a &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;live shark&lt;/a&gt; be cooler to take?&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-EFkMnteZDzw/VPX5rklkcWI/AAAAAAAABTI/GU2AL5ND0sY/s1600/Derek%2BHeasly%2Bupdated%2Bwatermark.png" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-EFkMnteZDzw/VPX5rklkcWI/AAAAAAAABTI/GU2AL5ND0sY/s1600/Derek%2BHeasly%2Bupdated%2Bwatermark.png" height="320" width="213" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Join &lt;a href="http://sharkdiver.com/"&gt;us&lt;/a&gt; for live shark selfie-taking starting this August at &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/dive-packages/great-white-shark-diving/"&gt;Guadalupe&lt;/a&gt;; &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/dive-packages/tiger-shark-diving/"&gt;Bahamas&lt;/a&gt; starting in April and &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/dive-packages/bull-shark-diving-fiji/"&gt;Fiji&lt;/a&gt; year-round.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Let's go shark diving!&lt;br /&gt;'Ocean'&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Shark Diver&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. term='Ocean advocate'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='island of the great white shark'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='Shark diving'/><title type='text'>Memorial announced for "Island of the Great White Shark" filmmaker, Richard Theiss</title><content type='html'>A memorial for Richard Theiss, our friend, underwater filmmaker and ocean advocate has been announced for 7 pm, March 20, 2015 at the aquarium of the pacific in Long Beach.&lt;br /&gt;&amp;nbsp; &lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;a href="https://scontent-lax.xx.fbcdn.net/hphotos-xpf1/v/t1.0-9/10370419_10206101974372027_4519600489715923870_n.jpg?oh=fda8414aceca5253927785cccc4f8554&amp;amp;oe=55909427" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="320" src="https://scontent-lax.xx.fbcdn.net/hphotos-xpf1/v/t1.0-9/10370419_10206101974372027_4519600489715923870_n.jpg?oh=fda8414aceca5253927785cccc4f8554&amp;amp;oe=55909427" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;His son Bryan posted this on his FB.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;i&gt;I'm pleased to share with Family, Friends, and Colleagues of Richard  Theiss, that a Memorial Service has been planned for Friday, March 20th @  7pm at the Aquarium of the Pacific in Long Beach, CA.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;i&gt; Please join us as we pay tribute to an incredibly thoughtful, caring and multi- talented man.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;i&gt; The Family would like to take a moment to thank Aquarium of the Pacific  CEO, Dr. Jerry Schubel, for his gracious hospitality in allowing us to  hold this Event.&amp;nbsp;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="text_exposed_show"&gt;&lt;i&gt; It's asked that  if you plan to attend the Memorial Service that you comment here or  message me directly so that we may gauge a guest count. However there  will be plenty of room and ALL are invited. reported today that &lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;Eugenie Clark, an American marine biologist who fell in love with sharks  as a child with her nose pressed against an aquarium tank—and whose  research on the much maligned species earned her the nickname "Shark  Lady"—died Wednesday morning in Sarasota, Florida. She was 92.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://images.nationalgeographic.com/wpf/media-content/photos/000/889/cache/88939_990x742-cb1424898755.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://images.nationalgeographic.com/wpf/media-content/photos/000/889/cache/88939_990x742-cb1424898755.jpg" height="320" width="209" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://images.nationalgeographic.com/wpf/media-content/photos/000/889/cache/88939_990x742-cb1424898755.jpg"&gt;Photograph by David Doubilet&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Eugenie Clark was an inspiration to generations of ocean explorers and had a special passion for sharks. She was one of the first to disspell&amp;nbsp; as stupid and deadly. After the movie "Jaws" hit the theaters, she wrote and article in National Geographic titled&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt; "Sharks: Magnificent and Misunderstood."&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;You can read the National Geographic obituary &lt;a href="http://news.nationalgeographic.com/news/2015/02/150225-eugenie-clark-shark-lady-marine-biologist-obituary-science/"&gt;here&lt;/a&gt;&amp;nbsp; and you can find out more about this inspirational woman &lt;a href="http://www.sharksider.com/eugenie-clark/"&gt;here&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Thank you Eugenie, for your passion and inspiration. I hope you're out there exploring new worlds.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Cheers,&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Martin Graf&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;CEO &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Shark Diver&amp;nbsp;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;i&gt; &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. Paul Watson of sea shepherd infamy is explaining in staggering scientific fashion (sharkasm intended), why the number of shark attacks seems to be increasing. Watson is saying:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;"Shark attacks are on the rise and the reason for this is entirely the fault of humanity."&amp;nbsp;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;To start with, we are diminishing bio-diversity in the ocean.  Overfishing has removed 90% of the fish from the sea since 1950. Every  single commercial fishery is in a state of decline. This is not just bad  news for humans who eat fish, but it is very bad news for sharks,  orcas, whales, seals and dolphins who have no choice but to eat fish.   In other words, starvation is a very big motivation for opportunistic  attacks.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Hmm, what!? Because there are not enough fish, sharks are attacking humans? Wait, didn't I hear that the seal populations are increasing and&lt;/span&gt;&lt;i&gt; &lt;/i&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;GWS as well as Orcas eat seals?&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://sharkfacts.org/wp-content/uploads/2009/03/shark-eating-seal-300x254.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://sharkfacts.org/wp-content/uploads/2009/03/shark-eating-seal-300x254.jpg" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://sharkfacts.org/wp-content/uploads/2009/03/shark-eating-seal-300x254.jpg"&gt;source&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&lt;br /&gt;While I was contemplating on how to disseminate and respond to this stellar piece of fiction writing, I saw that &lt;a href="https://www.blogger.com/profile/06787762757245289307"&gt;DaShark&lt;/a&gt; beat me to it. He is doing it much more eloquently than I ever could &lt;a href="http://fijisharkdiving.blogspot.com/2015/02/the-ocean-is-no-place-for-ignorant.html"&gt;here&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;In his colorful way, DaShark reasons: &lt;span style="color: purple;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;What a load of horseshit - predator/prey cycles anybody? And are we only  decimating the prey - or is it not rather so that we have  disproportionally targeted predator populations among which the Sharks?&amp;nbsp;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: purple;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The truth is that there is not one single documented case of more Shark attacks occurring because of overfishing!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;In fact, when it comes to some GWS populations, we may be experiencing the exact opposite! Having protected  the Pinnipeds, we are now seeing more GWS in California, the East Coast  of the USA and also Western Australia! And there are authoritative  voices claiming that the Tiger Shark population of Hawaii may be  increasing owing to the protection of Sea Turtles!&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: purple;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;That is only part of his blog. You can read the rest of what he has to say &lt;a href="http://fijisharkdiving.blogspot.com/2015/02/the-ocean-is-no-place-for-ignorant.html"&gt;here&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;i&gt; &lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Once again, excellent insight DaShark!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cheers,&lt;br /&gt;Martin Graf&lt;br /&gt;CEO &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Shark Diver&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.   As a global leader in commercial shark diving and conservation initiatives Shark Diver has spent the past decade engaged for sharks around the world. Our blog highlights all aspects of both of these dynamic and shifting worlds. in &lt;a href="http://www.sandiego.gov/"&gt;San Diego&lt;/a&gt; aired a nice report on the &lt;a href="http://scripps.ucsd.edu/"&gt;Scripps Institution of Oceanography&lt;/a&gt; and my friend Phil Zerofski, chief collector at the institute and owner of &lt;a href="http://www.seacamp.com/"&gt;Seacamp San Diego&lt;/a&gt;. They are using stuff they find in the ocean for all kinds of research, including curing cancers.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;iframe allowfullscreen="" frameborder="0" height="315" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/zu0bPXIR7ug" width="560"&gt;&lt;/iframe&gt; &lt;br /&gt;I got my start as a SCUBA instructor with &lt;a href="http://www.seacamp.com/"&gt;Seacamp San Diego&lt;/a&gt; and still work with their summer camp every year. If you have a kid that's  interested in marine sciences, I can highly recommend their summer  programs. They are not only educational, but a lot of fun to boot. Many  lifelong friendships have started there, including some of mine.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="https://scontent-a-dfw.xx.fbcdn.net/hphotos-xfp1/t31.0-8/10861104_10153067761916112_7163624543784224440_o.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="229" src="https://scontent-a-dfw.xx.fbcdn.net/hphotos-xfp1/t31.0-8/10861104_10153067761916112_7163624543784224440_o.jpg" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If you want more information on &lt;a href="https://www.facebook.com/SEACAMPSanDiego"&gt;Seacamp San Diego&lt;/a&gt;, visit their website at &lt;a href="http://www.seacamp.com/"&gt;www.seacamp.com&lt;/a&gt; or call them at 1-800 SEACAMP&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;By the way, in the video they say that Phil is diving to 1200ft, they should have said 12 meters or about 40 ft. &lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cheers,&lt;br /&gt;Martin Graf&lt;br /&gt;CEO Shark Diver&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. width='72'/><thr:total>0</thr:total></entry><entry><id>tag:blogger.com,1999:blog-370711998877298323.post-993863690559208325</id><published>2015-02-11T14:48:00.000-08:00</published><updated>2015-02-11T15:11:13.040-08:00</updated><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='shark diver'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='reef world'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='ocean conservancy'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='patric douglas'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='diving with sharks'/><title type='text'>Former Shark Diver CEO saving the Oceans?</title><content type='html'>Since I took over &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Shark Diver&lt;/a&gt; from &lt;a href="https://www.linkedin.com/in/patricdouglas"&gt;Patric Douglas &lt;/a&gt;on January 1 2012, he's been a very busy fellow. I'll let him tell you personally what he's been up to. Never one to follow the herd, he has used the same vision that has turned &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/bookings"&gt;Shark Diver&lt;/a&gt; into the premier shark diving company, to create his next project.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cheers,&lt;br /&gt;Martin Graf&lt;br /&gt;CEO Shark Diver&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So here is what Patric has been up to, in &lt;a href="http://artificialreefdesign.blogspot.com/2015/02/an-ex-shark-diving-ceos-second-act.html"&gt;his own words&lt;/a&gt;. &lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: left;"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-AUpKMR14pt4/VNqDa5cFEtI/AAAAAAAABBU/zTwOFYJjPfM/s1600/DSC_7410.JPG" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-AUpKMR14pt4/VNqDa5cFEtI/AAAAAAAABBU/zTwOFYJjPfM/s1600/DSC_7410.JPG" height="212" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;I consider myself to be one of the &lt;a href="https://www.linkedin.com/in/patricdouglas" target="_blank"&gt;luckiest fellows&lt;/a&gt; ever to have welded up a shark cage and set forth on the high seas of the Pacific to make my fortunes.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Well, it didn't quite happen like that, but 12 years ago the world was a different place.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Social media had yet to be born, digital cameras were still in development, and smartphones were still dumb phones...oh and people hated sharks.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Seems a bit anachronistic now, people hating sharks, but believe me 12 years ago welding up a shark cage was a really big deal.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So was the thought of creating a thriving commercial shark diving business 210 miles off the coast of Mexico at a tiny speck of land called Isla Guadalupe. But thanks to some fellow adventurers, one of them being &lt;a href="https://www.linkedin.com/pub/greg-grivetto/2a/41/b88" target="_blank"&gt;Greg Grivetto&lt;/a&gt;&amp;nbsp;with Horizon Charters, we forged ourselves into one of the best little shark diving companies on the planet - &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/" target="_blank"&gt;Shark Diver&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-Mw5BoT_RGOg/UiEE9Oj_EgI/AAAAAAAAAOo/SgKe0QWz41I/s1600/%2356.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-Mw5BoT_RGOg/UiEE9Oj_EgI/AAAAAAAAAOo/SgKe0QWz41I/s1600/%2356.jpg" height="240" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;For the next decade I had the time of my life. Who would not want to be in the company of simply Titanic sharks each year and call that a job? Additionally, I got to name a few like Shredder (now departed) and Kimel.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;We created a few &lt;a href="http://sharkfriendlymarinas.org/" target="_blank"&gt;unique conservation programs&lt;/a&gt; along the way, started a few shark tagging and research programs, did a lot of &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdivers.com/" target="_blank"&gt;cool film and TV&lt;/a&gt;, and I dabbled in a blog that pissed off absolutely everyone in the now growing, "shark diving industry."&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Let me say a few words about that.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;With few exceptions, most everything I wrote about over those many years has come to pass. I came into the shark world as a seasoned tourism and travel veteran having run 21 day tours all over good mother earth. Through those travels I got to see tourism and travel development in many countries including wild animal tourism development grow and thrive and...in many cases go wrong.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The shark diving world was growing and changing, my goal was to be a voice, and it was a great time to have a voice - at the very beginning.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Fast forward to 2012. It had now been well over a decade in the shark biz, the industry had grown and was in the middle of the 'teenage years' with social media adept youngsters trying to make their mark with sharks by riding them in bikinis - or &lt;a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=JmxxOBd3VMk" target="_blank"&gt;putting bird cages on their heads&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I have never been a fan of teenagers, or their antics, and that got me thinking.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Was I going to spend the rest of my life with sharks?&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The answer, as it tuned out, was a resounding - no.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I have always been one to tackle big things in life. To tread boldly where few have gone before and to create, build, and develop new ideas and new ways of doing things. So I traded &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Shark Diver&lt;/a&gt; for a very big bag of cash (thanks &lt;a href="http://www.facebook.com/whitesharkdiver"&gt;Martin Graf&lt;/a&gt;) and contemplated an Ex-Shark Diving CEO's Second Act. &lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="float: left; margin-right: 1em; text-align: left;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-TNn2878KTFA/VNp8gTjFsyI/AAAAAAAABBE/cU0dYKer2uw/s1600/Reef%2BWorlds%2BReef%2BStatues%2B-%2BCopy.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"&gt;&lt;img alt="" border="0" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-TNn2878KTFA/VNp8gTjFsyI/AAAAAAAABBE/cU0dYKer2uw/s1600/Reef%2BWorlds%2BReef%2BStatues%2B-%2BCopy.jpg" height="224" title="" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;Next BIG oceans idea - saving reefs - with design&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;A second act is a tall order, you do not always succeed, you sometimes fail, but you always learn.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;At the ripe old age of 46 I am more about success than failure so I got the idea for &lt;a href="http://www.reefworlds.com/" target="_blank"&gt;Reef Worlds&lt;/a&gt; and went from there.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So here's the BIG IDEA.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Near shore resort reefs are in severe decline around the world. This is best exampled by the Caribbean where close to 80% of reefs are in decline or gone completely.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;What *if* resorts around the world treated their near shore reefs as they did with their landscaping, what if they actually considered the oceans past the high tide mark offering an estimated 500 million tourists each year a chance to interact, become educated, and save the oceans at the same time?&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;To accomplish this resorts would need an incentive. Their new house reefs would have to be fully monetized because resort developers and resort management companies like Starwood do not do anything that does not add to the bottom line - and rightfully so.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This was the brainchild behind Reef Worlds. Re imagining what denuded house reefs could be, could look like, and could do for regional habitat with artificial reefs or as we call them - Dynamic Reefs.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Not all resorts need reef rehabilitation, but as we discovered in Dubai, &lt;a href="http://www.telegraph.co.uk/travel/destinations/middleeast/dubai/10937905/The-worlds-largest-underwater-theme-park-planned-in-Dubai.html" target="_blank"&gt;whole coastlines without reefs &lt;/a&gt;are a perfect match for what we had in mind and it's working.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So, this is what an Ex-Shark Diving CEO does with his time, that and fly fish, or dabble in wave power companies, and yes I am writing a blog. But cringe not dear reader for no one on this blog is taken to task.The funny thing about coral people, none of them wear bird cages on their heads and all of them are struggling mightily to save reefs with simply great ideas.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Kind of like where the shark world was back in 2003 when an out of sight, out of mind problem called "shark finning" was the big issue of the day.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;We can choose to sit on the sidelines and watch things change, or we can be the agents of change. Let me tell you, being a change agent is a lot of fun, once you try it, it will change your life forever.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Patric Douglas CEO&lt;br /&gt;Reef Worlds&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-OSEjfDBtC7w/VNqXKKXBj1I/AAAAAAAABBk/V1lgzAE-g6I/s1600/reef%2Bworlds%2Blogo.png" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-OSEjfDBtC7w/VNqXKKXBj1I/AAAAAAAABBk/V1lgzAE-g6I/s1600/reef%2Bworlds%2Blogo.png" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-OSEjfDBtC7w/VNqXKKXBj1I/AAAAAAAABBk/V1lgzAE-g6I/s1600/reef%2Bworlds%2Blogo.png" height="119" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.   As a global leader in commercial shark diving and conservation initiatives Shark Diver has spent the past decade engaged for sharks around the world. Our blog highlights all aspects of both of these dynamic and shifting worlds. term='swimming with sharks'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='shark tourism'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='volunteer with sharks'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='fiji'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='Shark diving'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='bull sharks'/><title type='text'>Volunteer opportunity for shark conservation in Fiji</title><content type='html'>Our friends at &lt;a href="http://www.projects-abroad.net/"&gt;Projects Abroad&lt;/a&gt; have an opportunity to volunteer with their shark conservation program in Fiji. This is an awesome project and I can personally vouch for the fact that you will have the time of your life, doing something worthwhile. I had the privilege to go along on a tagging trip and it was a ton of fun.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;This is their posting: &lt;/span&gt;&lt;i&gt;This is truly the chance of a life time to work on pioneering shark  protection projects alongside respected scientists and shark research  experts.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;object width="352" height="292" class="BLOG_video_class" id="BLOG_video-768e3ff55ee27f0c" classid="clsid:D27CDB6E-AE6D-11cf-96B8-444553540000" codebase="http://download.macromedia.com/pub/shockwave/cabs/flash/swflash.cab#version=6,0,40,0"&gt;&lt;param name="movie" src="//www.youtube.com/get_player" type="application/x-shockwave-flash" width="352" height="292" bgcolor="#FFFFFF" flashvars="flvurl=https://redirector.googlevideo.com/videoplayback?requiressl%3Dyes%26id%3D768e3ff55ee27f0c%26itag%3D5%26source%3Dblogger%26app%3Dblogger%26cmo%3Dsecure_transport%253Dyes%26cmo%3Dsensitive_content%253Dyes%26ip%3D0.0.0.0%26ipbits%3D0%26expire%3D1495466274%26sparams%3Drequiressl,id,itag,source,ip,ipbits,expire%26signature%3D7212E77F83A37F4720A542FF3A53615B7B88AF55.4E770B4BBE1C02B6D8B5F08947085AC84B36B0C4%26key%3Dck2&amp;iurl=http://video.google.com/ThumbnailServer2?app%3Dblogger%26contentid%3D768e3ff55ee27f0c%26offsetms%3D5000%26itag%3Dw160%26sigh%3Dq6gpUEMDWiThnb76M7KowBzaljc&amp;autoplay=0&amp;ps=blogger" allowFullScreen="true" /&gt;&lt;/object&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;This  project is perfect for anyone with a passion for marine wildlife and  the great outdoors. The Fiji Shark Conservation Project offers you the  chance to get up close to some of the most endangered and mis-understood  animals in the world. Volunteers are welcome on a gap year, a career  break, for university research, or even as an opportunity to experience a  very different way of life!&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.projects-abroad.co.uk/_photos/volunteer-projects/conservation-and-environment/shark-conservation/fiji/diving-with-sharks.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img alt="Diving with sharks" border="0" class="right-align" src="http://www.projects-abroad.co.uk/_photos/volunteer-projects/conservation-and-environment/shark-conservation/fiji/diving-with-sharks.jpg" title="Diving with sharks" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;Working directly with the Fiji Shark  Conservation Project, conducting the work of internationally renowned  shark research scientists, volunteers will be directly involved in  scientific shark research work, as well as actively working within the  local community on mangrove reforestation, recycling and shark education  initiatives. The volunteers and the conservation work are supervised by  our resident marine biologist and local staff. We also work closely  with other local and international marine conservation organisations,  including the WWF Global Shark Programme.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;The project is based in Pacific Harbour, on the south coast of Fiji’s main island of Viti Levu, just 3 hours from Nadi.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-aTaARkgtMCU/Ux99UeqKoDI/AAAAAAAAAwg/JuMdWDcuiMM/s1600/safety%2Bstop%2Bfiji.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-aTaARkgtMCU/Ux99UeqKoDI/AAAAAAAAAwg/JuMdWDcuiMM/s1600/safety%2Bstop%2Bfiji.jpg" height="213" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;Volunteers  do not need any previous diving or shark research experience to take  part in the Fiji Conservation Project. However, volunteers need to be  able to swim, be medically fit to scuba dive and have a good command of  the English language to get the most out of the Shark Conservation  project. This project is not available for people who do not want to  take part in the diving.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: blue;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;Volunteers who have not dived before  receive the PADI Open Water dive course during their first two weeks on  the project. Volunteers with an existing dive certification equivalent  to the PADI Open Water qualification receive the PADI Advanced course.  After the dive course, volunteers will also receive the Project Aware  Shark Conservation Diver Course. Those who already have the Advanced  certification or higher will receive the Project Aware Shark  Conservation Diver Course during their first week, and an extra Shark  Feed Dive during their project time.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;You can get all the information on this link: &lt;a href="http://www.projects-abroad.co.uk/volunteer-projects/conservation-and-environment/shark-conservation/fiji/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;http://www.projects-abroad.co.uk/volunteer-projects/conservation-and-environment/shark-conservation/fiji/&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This project is of course at the same location we go to dive with &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/dive-packages/bull-shark-diving-fiji/"&gt;bull sharks&lt;/a&gt; in May. If you can't volunteer for this project, maybe you want to come out diving with us and support &lt;a href="http://fijisharkdive.com/"&gt;Beqa Adventure Divers&lt;/a&gt;, the outfit who was responsible for creating the first &lt;a href="http://fijisharkdiving.blogspot.com/2014/10/shark-reef-marine-reserve-breaking-news.html"&gt;underwater national park in Fiji&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-jlG8YSanWKE/U35NLo1fPsI/AAAAAAAAA5M/GK_PtPMYMk0/s1600/XD5V1869-293.JPG" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-jlG8YSanWKE/U35NLo1fPsI/AAAAAAAAA5M/GK_PtPMYMk0/s1600/XD5V1869-293.JPG" height="213" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Our trips are from May 9-17, 15-24 and 22-31. For more information call 619.887.4275, email us at staff@sharkdiver.com or visit us on the web &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/dive-packages/bull-shark-diving-fiji/"&gt;here&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Let's go to Fiji!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cheers,&lt;br /&gt;Martin Graf&lt;br /&gt;CEO &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Shark Diver&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.   As a global leader in commercial shark diving and conservation initiatives Shark Diver has spent the past decade engaged for sharks around the world. Our blog highlights all aspects of both of these dynamic and shifting worlds. season at &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/tv"&gt;Guadalupe Island&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;b&gt;&amp;nbsp; &lt;/b&gt;Our season runs from August to mid November and the position is full time during that time.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div id="stcpDiv" style="left: -1988px; &lt;/b&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The duties include the supervision of the divers, familiarizing the non-certified divers with the hookah gear, (discover scuba) ensuring the safety of the dive operation as well as general boat-crew work. He/she is also responsible for customer service, welcoming and checking in the guests, when they arrive on the boat. Additional duties include the production of a trip DVD and helping our divers with their gear.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The ideal candidate has a degree in, or is studying marine biology, has extensive experience diving with sharks, great customer service skills,&amp;nbsp; a basic knowledge of video and photo editing and prior live-aboard work experience. The ability to pay attention to details, adhere to established safety protocols and follow the directions of the captain are absolute must have's for the successful candidate. Teaching status, insured SCUBA instructor rating, with current first aid certification is also required.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Our vessel is registered and based in the US and all our crew members must be able to legally work here. A valid US passport/passport card, or a foreign passport with a valid work visa are required to work on the boat. No exceptions. &lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;We are offering a competitive salary, the opportunity to work with a great team and to get up close and personal with great white sharks. advocate.</title><content type='html'>&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: left;"&gt;Yesterday, we lost Richard Theiss, a nice guy and great underwater filmmaker. His son Bryan posted the following on his facebook page.&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: left;"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: data-ft="{&amp;quot;tn&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;K&amp;quot;}" id="fbPhotoSnowliftCaption" tabindex="0"&gt;&lt;span class="hasCaption"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="https://scontent-lax1-1.xx.fbcdn.net/hphotos-xpf1/v/t1.0-9/10996487_10202533754904784_6640793239172365852_n.jpg?oh=66777e5e5f0664a07b55aacd1ceb982e&amp;amp;oe=55E836A7" imageanchor="1" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;span class="fbPhotosPhotoCaption" data-ft="{&amp;quot;tn&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;K&amp;quot;}" id="fbPhotoSnowliftCaption" tabindex="0"&gt;&lt;span class="hasCaption"&gt;&lt;br /&gt; Today I lost my Father, Best Friend, Unwavering Supporter and Mentor.  The world lost today a Musician, Oceanographer, Wildlife Conservationist  and Animal Rights Activist. The Heavens gained today the most  Compassionate, Sincere, Caring, and Thoughtful person I've ever known. I  miss you with every breath Dad!&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;span class="fbPhotosPhotoCaption" data-ft="{&amp;quot;tn&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;*G&amp;quot;,&amp;quot;type&amp;quot;:45}" id="fbPhotoPageCaption" tabindex="0"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;span class="fbPhotosPhotoCaption" data-ft="{&amp;quot;tn&amp;quot;:&amp;quot;*G&amp;quot;,&amp;quot;type&amp;quot;:45}" id="fbPhotoPageCaption" tabindex="0"&gt;&lt;span class="hasCaption"&gt;The  Family would like to welcome any Photos, Stories and Memories you'd  like to share. You are welcome to post here, private message me them  directly, or email me at brtheiss@msn.com&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;span class="fbPhotoTagList" id="fbPhotoPageTagList"&gt;&lt;span class="fcg"&gt; &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: left;"&gt;I've know Richard for over a decade and remember him for his love of the &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/dive-packages/great-white-shark-diving/"&gt;Great White Sharks&lt;/a&gt;. He came out with us for many, many expeditions, filming his documentary &lt;a href="http://www.cadivingnews.com/article/116/Island-of-the-Great-White-Shark"&gt;"Island of the Great White Shark"&lt;/a&gt;. We shared some good times, over the years and I remember him always asking about his favorite shark "Mystery"&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: left;"&gt;&lt;span id="goog_1960964027"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span id="goog_1960964028"&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: left;"&gt;The last time I saw Richard was last year, when he told me that he was looking forward to spending time with his son Bryan in Hawaii. Sadly that time turned out to be much too short.&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: left;"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: left;"&gt;Richard, you will be missed my friend!&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: left;"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: left;"&gt;Cheers,&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: left;"&gt;Martin Graf&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: left;"&gt;CEO Shark Diver &lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: left;"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.   As a global leader in commercial shark diving and conservation initiatives Shark Diver has spent the past decade engaged for sharks around the world. Our blog highlights all aspects of both of these dynamic and shifting worlds.
