imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="200" src="https://fbcdn-sphotos-c-a.akamaihd.net/hphotos-ak-xpa1/v/t1.0-9/10653533_10152426127849143_7145045692826401049_n.jpg?oh=cb5fe2efc6f93875a26897c542a007e9&amp;amp;oe=5566777E&amp;amp;__gda__=1431720552_3d28ea40fc21f7d25c5655ab2df0fe35" width="132" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;Every year we get hundreds of emails from people asking us, how they can get involved with &lt;a href="http://www.marinecsi.org/"&gt;shark research&lt;/a&gt;. This has lead to &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Shark Diver&lt;/a&gt; teaming up with Nicole Nasby-Lucas from &lt;a href="http://www.marinecsi.org/"&gt;MCSI&lt;/a&gt; to offer special &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/dive-packages/great-white-shark-diving/"&gt;science expeditions&lt;/a&gt; to &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/tv/"&gt;Guadalupe Island&lt;/a&gt;. These special science expedition give our divers a chance to actively participate in the &lt;a href="http://www.marinecsi.org/white-shark/"&gt;Great White Shark photo ID&lt;/a&gt; project and also learn about the results of various studies, involving our sharks at Isla Guadalupe.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The response from our divers has been overwhelming. Last year's science expeditions filled up in just a couple of weeks and for this season, we already sold out our September and October expeditions. Right now, we do have a a few spaces left on our November 11-16 expedition.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-9XDvtzxmpGQ/UrNkY-pdkBI/AAAAAAAAAmQ/ppgxQLgiigI/s1600/sharks+2006+193.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-9XDvtzxmpGQ/UrNkY-pdkBI/AAAAAAAAAmQ/ppgxQLgiigI/s320/sharks+2006+193.jpg" height="229" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;Don't miss your chance to be part of this exciting research, which up to today has resulted in over 160 sharks being identified at Guadalupe Island. Some individuals like "Bite Face", "Jaques", "Thor" and "Chugey" are regular visitors and have been seen every year since we started going to &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/dive-packages/great-white-shark-diving/"&gt;Guadalupe Island&lt;/a&gt;. You will learn the differences in behavior and migration between male, female, juvenile and adult sharks along with many other interesting things about Great White Sharks and sharks in general.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Nicole has a wealth of information and is excited about sharing her knowledge with you, our divers and research assistants. She will teach you how to identify the individual sharks and tell you about their history at &lt;a href="http://www.sharkiver.com/tv"&gt;Guadalupe Island&lt;/a&gt;. Just imagine, next time you watch "shark week", you might recognize the shark and realize that it's the one you came face to face with. The one that looked you straight into the eyes!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="https://fbcdn-sphotos-c-a.akamaihd.net/hphotos-ak-xaf1/t31.0-8/s960x960/1502275_10152531005044143_1774142672793037622_o.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="clear: left; float: left; margin-bottom: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="320" src="https://fbcdn-sphotos-c-a.akamaihd.net/hphotos-ak-xaf1/t31.0-8/s960x960/1502275_10152531005044143_1774142672793037622_o.jpg" width="253" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;If you would like to be part of this experience, we recommend that you book now, since this is your last chance to join a scientific expedition in 2015.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The price for this trip of a lifetime is $3300 and it includes &lt;span class="userContent"&gt;a copy of the photo ID book, containing all the identified  sharks at &lt;a href="http://sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Isla Guadalupe&lt;/a&gt;. We will also provide digital underwater cameras for you to use and you'll get a DVD of your trip to take home and share with your friends. If we encounter a new shark during your expedition, the group will be offered and opportunity to name the shark!&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span class="userContent"&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span class="userContent"&gt;This special &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/dive-packages/great-white-shark-diving-science-expedition/"&gt;science expedition&lt;/a&gt; will run from &lt;b&gt;September 11-16 2015&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span class="userContent"&gt;To book your expedition, or for more information, call us toll free at 855.987.4275 or  619.887.4275. You can also reach us via email at staff@sharkdiver.com or visit &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/dive-packages/great-white-shark-diving-science-expedition/"&gt;http://www.sharkdiver.com/dive-packages/great-white-shark-diving-science-expedition/&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span class="userContent"&gt;Let's go shark diving!&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span class="userContent"&gt;Cheers!&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span class="userContent"&gt;Martin Graf&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span class="userContent"&gt;CEO&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span class="userContent"&gt;Shark Diver&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span class="userContent"&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. Diver&lt;/a&gt;&lt;b&gt; &lt;/b&gt;and Emmy award winning underwater cinematographer Peter Kragh at the peak of &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/tv"&gt;Isla Guadalupe&lt;/a&gt;'s&lt;b&gt; Whether you are just an amateur or an emerging filmmaker, this is an opportunity to get some expert tips to improve your videos and, of course, see some of the greatest sharks in the world.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/01/Peter-Kragh.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://www.sharkdiver.com/wp-content/uploads/2015/01/Peter-Kragh.jpg" height="212" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;Peter Kragh&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;Peter is intimately familiar with sharks. There will also be screenings of some of Peters work. With all his diving experience from around the world, Peter can also help you find that "secret" location for your next diving adventure.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Here is a short video, showcasing Peter's work.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;iframe allowfullscreen="" frameborder="0" height="281" mozallowfullscreen="" src="//player.vimeo.com/video/94559582" webkitallowfullscreen="" width="500"&gt;&lt;/iframe&gt; &lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://vimeo.com/94559582"&gt;Demo Reel 2014&lt;/a&gt; from &lt;a href="http://vimeo.com/peterkragh"&gt;Peter Kragh&lt;/a&gt; on &lt;a href="https://vimeo.com/"&gt;Vimeo&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;As a professional cameraman for over 10 years, Peter has worked on well known BBC and National Geographic projects like Blue Planet, Planet Earth, Life and Secret Life of Predators. In 2013 he won an Emmy award for outstanding cinematography on the Nat Geo series "Untamed Americas". He has also worked on multiple Imax films: Deep Sea 3D, Hubble 3D, Under The Sea 3D, and Journey to the South Pacific 3D.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;With all his experience filming both underwater and topside, you are sure to learn a lot from Peter. This is a unique opportunity to both improve your filming skills and have an experience of a lifetime, coming face to face with the &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/dive-packages/great-white-shark-diving/"&gt;Great White Sharks&lt;/a&gt; at &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/tv"&gt;Isla Guadalupe.&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-Mw5BoT_RGOg/UiEE9Oj_EgI/AAAAAAAAAOo/SgKe0QWz41I/s1600/%2356.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-Mw5BoT_RGOg/UiEE9Oj_EgI/AAAAAAAAAOo/SgKe0QWz41I/s1600/%2356.jpg" height="240" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Come join us and Peter on either September 4-9 2015 or September 9-14 2015 for a trip of a lifetime.&lt;br /&gt;Cost is $3,300 for a 5 day live aboard trip, leaving from and returning to San Diego. &lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;For more information visit &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/dive-packages/great-white-shark-diving-film-expedition/"&gt;www.sharkdiver.com/dive-packages/great-white-shark-diving-film-expedition/&lt;/a&gt; or call us at 619.887.4275 toll free 855.987.4275 email staff@sharkdiver.com&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;You can also contact us via our website &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com//bookings/"&gt;http://www.sharkdiver.com//bookings/&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I hope to see you this in September.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Let's go shark diving!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cheers,&lt;br /&gt;Martin Graf&lt;br /&gt;CEO Shark Diver&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div id="stcpDiv" style="left: -1988px; position: absolute; top: -1999px;"&gt;Peter  is intimately familiar with sharks. scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='shark diver'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='cage diving'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='guadalupe cage diving'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='guadalupe island'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='great white shark'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='shark ID'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='Shark diving'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='shredder the shark'/><title type='text'>The "baddest" shark at Isla Guadalupe?</title><content type='html'>&lt;br /&gt;I want to introduce you to some of the sharks we have met over the last 14 years at &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/tv"&gt;Guadalupe Island&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;br /&gt;Thanks to the &lt;a href="http://www.marinecsi.org/white-shark/"&gt;Photo Id&lt;/a&gt; project we are able to individually identify the sharks and keep track of who's visiting the Island each year. We are now at over 155 different sharks, some of them having been seen at Guadalupe every years, since we started going there in 2001.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;A couple of weeks ago, I wrote about the ID project &lt;a href="http://sharkdivers.blogspot.com/2015/01/how-do-we-identify-sharks-at-guadalupe.html"&gt;here&lt;/a&gt; and now I want to start out by introducing you to the guy who got me hooked on shark diving.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-5dyAfdBCWQo/VMpiUFb2dWI/AAAAAAAABP4/G77yGLA0xbY/s1600/Shredder%2B1.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-5dyAfdBCWQo/VMpiUFb2dWI/AAAAAAAABP4/G77yGLA0xbY/s1600/Shredder%2B1.jpg" height="145" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;"Shredder"&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;"Shredder" was one of the real characters at &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/tv"&gt;Guadalupe Island&lt;/a&gt;. Never the most careful shark, he definitely kept us entertained an on our toes. Most divers recognized him by his shredded dorsal fin. While some called him "Scar" and others "Cal Ripfin", to me, he has always been "Shredder". Most people think that he got his name because of his "shredded" dorsal fin. That is actually not the case. He got his name a few years before he "shredded" his fin. On the very first trip to &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/tv"&gt;Guadalupe Island&lt;/a&gt; one of the divers went up to the captain of the &lt;a href="http://www.horizoncharters.com/"&gt;"Horizon"&lt;/a&gt; and told him "A shark just bit through your anchor line". Knowing how thick the anchor line is, the captain doubted that the shark bit all the way through it and went to the bow, to check things out. There were indeed just a few feet of anchor line dangling over the&amp;nbsp; rail and just as he got there a shark jumped up, trying to get the rest. .... that is how "Shredder" got his name, he shredded the anchor line.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" height="212" src="https://fbcdn-sphotos-g-a.akamaihd.net/hphotos-ak-xap1/v/t1.0-9/76887_453535139142_509043_n.jpg?oh=4d106917a326e5bf127f0b1696828e0a&amp;amp;oe=556B9C5E&amp;amp;__gda__=1432712059_1c4f017f1ff792e143f7fcc616236d34" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;"Shredder's unique dorsal fin"&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;Biting anchor lines were not the only thing he was famous for. He loved showing off for our divers. On one particular day, he kept swimming back and forth, just inches from the cages for 7 solid hours. It was during a day, where we couldn't put any attractant or baits into the water. That didn't stop him from checking out our divers all day long.&amp;nbsp; Swimming by the cages, looking each diver in the eyes, the exactly how he got me hooked on shark diving.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-GZZwEdUFoDI/VMpcSFOvAgI/AAAAAAAABPo/SqnPz1QgwMU/s1600/P1000094.JPG" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-GZZwEdUFoDI/VMpcSFOvAgI/AAAAAAAABPo/SqnPz1QgwMU/s1600/P1000094.JPG" height="240" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;Hi I'm Shredder!&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;&amp;nbsp;Another thing that made "Shredder" unique was the fact that he didn't seem to have gotten the memo that &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/dive-packages/great-white-shark-diving/"&gt;great white sharks&lt;/a&gt; have a hierarchy based on size. Normally, the smaller sharks defers to the bigger ones, but not Shredder. He was definitely not intimidated by anyone.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;table align="center" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="tr-caption-container" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;tbody&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td style="text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-4Nofx2bItQI/VMpYt9mqloI/AAAAAAAABPY/3eCv0kCVi5o/s1600/n581295954_1199900_8062.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-4Nofx2bItQI/VMpYt9mqloI/AAAAAAAABPY/3eCv0kCVi5o/s1600/n581295954_1199900_8062.jpg" height="212" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;tr&gt;&lt;td class="tr-caption" style="text-align: center;"&gt;Shredder with Dr. "Mau"&lt;/td&gt;&lt;/tr&gt;&lt;/tbody&gt;&lt;/table&gt;He was also a shark that loved to breach! I have seen him do that at least 5 or 6 times. &lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;"Shredder" was at &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/tv"&gt;Guadalupe Island &lt;/a&gt;from 2001 to 2012 and hasn't been seen since then. I don't know what happened to him. Maybe he got caught by a fishing boat, maybe he didn't defer to a bigger shark and died. I prefer to think that he's still out there, swimming in the vast oceans and will return some day. It's not unprecedented that a shark stays away from Guadalupe for years at a time. We had one show up after an absence of 8 years.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If you want to come out with us and see if "Shredder" returns this season, call us at 855.987.4275 or visit &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com//bookings/"&gt;http://www.sharkdiver.com//bookings/&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Let's go shark diving!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cheers,&lt;br /&gt;Martin Graf&lt;br /&gt;CEO &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Shark Diver&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.   As a global leader in commercial shark diving and conservation initiatives Shark Diver has spent the past decade engaged for sharks around the world. Our blog highlights all aspects of both of these dynamic and shifting worlds. You can reach us directly at staff@sharkdiver.com.</content><link rel='replies' type='application/atom+xml' href='https://sharkdivers.blogspot.com/feeds/4818068858992568796/comments/default' title='Post Comments'/><link rel='replies' type='text/html' href='https://www.blogger.com/comment.g?blogID=370711998877298323&amp;postID=4818068858992568796' title='2 Comments'/><link rel='edit' type='application/atom+xml' href='https://www.blogger.com/feeds/370711998877298323/posts/default/4818068858992568796'/><link rel='self' type='application/atom+xml' href='https://www.blogger.com/feeds/370711998877298323/posts/default/4818068858992568796'/><link rel='alternate' type='text/html' href='http://sharkdivers.blogspot.com/2015/01/the-baddest-shark-at-isla-guadalupe.html' title='The &quot;baddest&quot; shark at Isla Guadalupe?'/><author><name>Shark Diver</name><uri>https://plus.google.com/107965598445039841723</uri><email>noreply@blogger.com</email><gd:image rel='http://schemas.google.com/g/2005#thumbnail' width='32' height='32' src='//lh5.googleusercontent.com/-acNbaifFSTQ/AAAAAAAAAAI/AAAAAAAAB_A/inqVjDI-1J8/s32-c/photo.jpg'/></author><media:thumbnail xmlns:media='http://search.yahoo.com/mrss/' url='http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-5dyAfdBCWQo/VMpiUFb2dWI/AAAAAAAABP4/G77yGLA0xbY/s72-c/Shredder%2B1.jpg' height='72' width='72'/><thr:total>2</thr:total></entry><entry><id>tag:blogger.com,1999:blog-370711998877298323.post-538438000809300026</id><published>2015-01-20T16:37:00.000-08:00</published><updated>2015-01-20T17:04:31.745-08:00</updated><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='stupid shark policy'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='tourism killer'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='environment'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='australia'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='Shark diving'/><category scheme='http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#' term='eco tourism'/><title type='text'>Australia. Sabotaging Eco Tourism?</title><content type='html'>I hate to say it, but Australia is at it again. After &lt;a href="http://sharkdivers.blogspot.com/2014/12/really-western-australia-again.html"&gt;hunting down&lt;/a&gt; a tagged &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;shark&lt;/a&gt; for simply being too close to shore, they now have declared their intention to "opt out of protections for 5 shark species".&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-jszMggXMYYI/VL7ysgB2XDI/AAAAAAAABOI/bAtDvRABD6U/s1600/untitled-4051.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-jszMggXMYYI/VL7ysgB2XDI/AAAAAAAABOI/bAtDvRABD6U/s1600/untitled-4051.jpg" height="213" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.theguardian.com/"&gt;The guardian&lt;/a&gt; writes that &lt;span style="color: #6fa8dc;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="color: #0b5394;"&gt;The government is submitting a “reservation” against three species of  thresher shark and two species of hammerhead shark listed as protected  migratory species under the UN-administered&lt;/span&gt; &lt;a class=" u-underline" data-component="in-body-link" data-link-name="in body link" href="http://www.cms.int/"&gt;convention on the conservation of migratory species of wild animals&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="color: #6fa8dc;"&gt;&lt;b&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;span style="color: #0b5394;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: #0b5394;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;The five types of shark were among 31 species granted new protection  status at a convention summit in November. A record 21 species of shark  and ray, including sawfish, were put on the list along with polar bears,  whales and gazelles.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: #0b5394;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: #0b5394;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;Although Australia did not object to the listings in November, it is  now seeking to opt out of the commitment to cooperate with other  countries to ensure the five migratory shark species do not become  extinct. The expanded list is due to come into effect on 8 February.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;div class="separator" style="clear: both; text-align: center;"&gt;&lt;a href="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-LFOS1CjzCaU/VL70VNmaYCI/AAAAAAAABOU/EJnN90eU1ag/s1600/untitled-4035.jpg" imageanchor="1" style="margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 1em;"&gt;&lt;img border="0" src="http://3.bp.blogspot.com/-LFOS1CjzCaU/VL70VNmaYCI/AAAAAAAABOU/EJnN90eU1ag/s1600/untitled-4035.jpg" height="213" width="320" /&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/div&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: #0b5394;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Since sharks are a vital part of a healthy ocean environment &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: #0b5394;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: #0b5394;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;it seems that the government is not too concerned about&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt; losing all the tourists who visit Australia to dive and enjoy the incredible reefs they have. The only ones they care about is the fishermen. The article quotes &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: #0b5394;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Alexia Wellbelove, senior program manager at &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;a class=" u-underline" data-component="in-body-link" data-link-name="in body link" href="http://www.hsi.org.au/"&gt;Humane Society International&lt;/a&gt;&lt;span style="color: #6fa8dc;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;b&gt; &lt;span style="color: #0b5394;"&gt;"&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: #0b5394;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;the opt-out was to appease commercial and recreational fishers, some of  whom catch threshers and hammerhead sharks as primary catch or as  bycatch for other species.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;i&gt; &lt;span style="color: #0b5394;"&gt;“This is a political decision, it has nothing to do with conservation,  which is pretty pathetic really,” she said. “Australia has always spoken  out against other countries making reservations under these kinds of  treaties, so this move is really concerning.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: #0b5394;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;The article states &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;span style="color: #0b5394;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: #0b5394;"&gt;&lt;i&gt;"A spokesman for the federal environment minister, &lt;a class=" u-underline" data-component="auto-linked-tag" data-link-name="auto-linked-tag" href="http://www.theguardian.com/australia-news/greg-hunt"&gt;Greg Hunt&lt;/a&gt;,  said the government’s move was to avoid “unintended consequences” for  fishers in Australia, who would risk being fined up to $170,000 and face  two years in jail even if they obeyed their permits.&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/span&gt; &amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: #0b5394;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;So they say that their laws are too harsh for the fishermen who kill these sharks and instead of changing the punishment for the killing, they just kill the protection for these sharks. Sound reasoning indeed. (sharkasm intended)&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: #0b5394;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Read the entire article &lt;a href="http://www.theguardian.com/environment/2015/jan/20/australian-government-seeks-to-opt-out-of-protection-of-five-shark-species"&gt;here&lt;/a&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: #0b5394;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Dashark's reaction &lt;a href="http://fijisharkdiving.blogspot.com/2015/01/australia-environmental-vandalism.html"&gt;here&lt;/a&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: #0b5394;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;I recommend that you send your opinion to the Australian tourism website &lt;a href="http://www.australia.com/?cid=paid-search|us|us-local-fy2014|brand|yahoo|yahoo|textad|167-australia-broad|australia-tourism|broad|core||||#"&gt;here&lt;/a&gt; and click on the feedback link.&amp;nbsp; You can also visit their &lt;a href="https://www.facebook.com/SeeAustralia"&gt;Facebook page&lt;/a&gt; and leave a comment there.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: #0b5394;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;If the politicians won't listen to us, maybe their tourist board is more receptive.&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: #0b5394;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Cheers,&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: #0b5394;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;Martin Graf&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: #0b5394;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;CEO &lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;Shark Diver&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;span style="color: #0b5394;"&gt;&lt;span style="color: black;"&gt;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/span&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;span style="color: #0b5394;"&gt; &lt;/span&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://www.sharkdiver.com/"&gt;&lt;b&gt;About Shark Diver&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/a&gt;.   As a global leader in commercial shark diving and conservation initiatives Shark Diver has spent the past decade engaged for sharks around the world. Our blog highlights all aspects of both of these dynamic and shifting worlds. What really happened.</title><content type='html'>Shark Attack in Australia? Part 2&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;b&gt; &lt;/b&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Yesterday we talked about the teenager who got "attacked" by a shark &lt;a href="http://sharkdivers.blogspot.com/2015/01/shark-attack-in-australia.html"&gt;here&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Today he admits that it wasn't really the sharks fault. Watch the video below.&lt;br /&gt;Sam Smith now says that the shark would have ignored him, had he left him alone.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;object classid="clsid:D27CDB6E-AE6D-11cf-96B8-444553540000" codebase="http://download.macromedia.com/pub/shockwave/cabs/flash/swflash.cab#version=9,0,47,0" height="360" id="flashObj" width="540"&gt;&lt;param name="movie" value="http://c.brightcove.com/services/viewer/federated_f9?isVid=1&amp;isUI=1" /&gt;&lt;param name="bgcolor" value="#FFFFFF" /&gt;&lt;param name="flashVars" value="videoId=3995997839001&amp;playerID=3680665367001&amp;playerKey=AQ~~,AAACKW9LH8k~,A7HfECo5t7CatyA-8fEJ4LzBn7uU7ewe&amp;domain=embed&amp;dynamicStreaming=true" /&gt;&lt;param name="base" value="http://admin.brightcove.com" /&gt;&lt;param name="seamlesstabbing" value="false" /&gt;&lt;param name="allowFullScreen" value="true" /&gt;&lt;param name="swLiveConnect" value="true" /&gt;&lt;param name="allowScriptAccess" value="always" /&gt;&lt;embed src="http://c.brightcove.com/services/viewer/federated_f9?isVid=1&amp;isUI=1" bgcolor="#FFFFFF" flashVars="videoId=3995997839001&amp;playerID=3680665367001&amp;playerKey=AQ~~,AAACKW9LH8k~,A7HfECo5t7CatyA-8fEJ4LzBn7uU7ewe&amp;domain=embed&amp;dynamicStreaming=true" base="http://admin.brightcove.com" name="flashObj" width="540" height="360" seamlesstabbing="false" type="application/x-shockwave-flash" allowFullScreen="true" allowScriptAccess="always" swLiveConnect="true" pluginspage="http://www.macromedia.com/shockwave/download/index.cgi?P1_Prod_Version=ShockwaveFlash"&gt;&lt;/embed&gt;&lt;/object&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Funny, how the commentary still refers to it as an attack.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I'm glad the kid is going to be OK and that they reported what actually happened.
